+Jamison Brereton

48
Dawn
Praskaс╣Зva K─Бс╣Зva
16 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, arranged in prag─Бthas
Another in Praskaс╣Зva K─Бс╣ЗvaтАЩs series devoted to the deities of the early-morning sacrifice, this hymn to Dawn is especially concerned with the acquisition of goodsтАФ a common association because the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б or тАЬpriestly giftтАЭ is distributed to the poets and priests at the Morning Pressing. The radiant beauty of Dawn and her mandate to rouse and animate all living beings are not neglected in the hymn, how ever, especially in the middle verses (5тАУ10). In verses 11тАУ12 she is also, unusually, charged with a task more appropriate for Agni (see, e.g., I.44), namely conveying the gods to the sacrifice.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬUс╣гas, daughter of heaven, dawn upon us with riches; diffuser of light, dawn upon us with abundant food; bountiful goddess, dawn upon with wealth (of cattle).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Along with a thing of value, dawn forth to us, Daughter of Heaven, along with lofty brilliance, radiant goddess, along with wealth, (you who are) rich in gifts.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. uс╣гaс╕е was carelessly omitted in the published translation

+Griffith

DAWN on us with prosperity, O Usas, Daughter of the Sky,
Dawn with great glory, Goddess, Lady of the Light, dawn thou with riches, Bounteous One.

+Geldner

Mit Gl├╝ck leuchte uns auf, Usas, Tochter des Himmels, mit hohem Glanze, mit Reichtum freigebig, du strahlende G├╢ttin!

+Grassmann

Mit sch├╢nem Gut, o Morgenroth, o Himmelstochter leuchte uns, O strahlenreiche, du mit grosser Herrlichkeit, mit Reichthum, G├╢ttin, Geberin!

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAbounding with horses, abounding with kine, bestowers of every sort of wealth, (the divinities of morning) are possessed of much that is necessary for the habitations (of men); Uс╣гas, speak to me kind words; send us the affluence of the wealthy.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The epithets of Uс╣гas are in feminine plural, without a substantive: a┼Ыvavatiс╕е, gomatiс╕е, vi┼Ыvasuvidaс╕е; hence, assumed: uс╣гo-devataс╕е, the many divinities of dawn

+Jamison Brereton

Possessing horses and cows, finding all goods in abundance, (the dawns) bestir themselves to shine.
Arouse liberalities toward me, o Dawn; stimulate the generosity of the benefactors.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

With most tr./comm. I follow Bloomfield in interpr. vi┼Ыvasuv├нd- as haplology for *vi┼Ыva-vasu-v├нd-.

The p─Бda break favors taking bh┼л╠Бri with the verb, as most do (e.g., Geldner тАЬgeben sie sich viele M├╝heтАЭ), but semantically it goes better with p─Бda a. Cf. expressions like bh┼л╠Бri te v├бsu (I.81.2, 6, VIII.32.8), bh┼л╠Бri v─Б╠Бmam (I.124.12, VI.71.4), and esp.

bh┼л╠Бri тАж sa├║bhagam in 9c below.

On s┼лnс╣Ы╠Бt─Б- as тАШliberality, liberal (gifts)тАЩ, see RenouтАЩs discussion here (EVP III.17), summarizing previous work.

+Griffith

They, bringing steeds and kine, boon-givers of all wealth, have oft sped forth to lighten us.
O Usas, waken up for me the sounds of joy: send us the riches of the great.

+Geldner

Rossereich, rinderreich, alle Sch├дtze verschaffend, geben sie sich viele M├╝he, um aufzuleuchten. Hole f├╝r mich Schenkungen heraus, o Usas; sporne die Freigebigkeit der Lohnherren an!

+Grassmann

An Rossen reich und Rindern, spendend alles Gut sind oft zum Leuchten sie genaht; So send’ auch du mir reiches Gut, o Morgenroth; die F├╝rsten treib zum Schenken an.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe divine Uс╣гas has dwelt (in heaven of old); may she dawn today, the excitress of chariots which are harnessed at her coming, as those who are desirous of wealth (send ships) to sea.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Samudre na ┼Ыravasyavaс╕е = like those desirous of wealth for sea;

Added: ‘send ships’. uv─Бsa, uс╣гaс╕е is explained: pur─Б niv─Бsam akarot, she has made a dwelling formerly; an allusion to her producing the dawn, prabh─Бtam kс╣Ыtavat─л

+Jamison Brereton

Dawn has dawned (before) and will dawn nowтАФthe lively goddess of the chariots.
Those who hold themselves (ready [for giving]) at her approaches, as those who seek fame on the sea hold themselves (firm),

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Most tr. take j─лr─Б╠Бas agentive with an objective genitive (e.g., Geldner тАЬdie Wagen in Bewegung setzendтАЭ), but I think this unlikely because it would be the only such usage of j─лr├б-. (g├│-j─лra- in IX.110.3 is sometimes so interpreted [Geldner тАШdie K├╝he zutreibendтАЩ] but need not be.) Although not taking j─лr─Б╠Бas transitive leaves r├бth─Бn─Бm without any clear governing word, that seems preferable to claiming a unique value for j─лr├б- in this passage. That Dawn may be тАЬthe lady of the chariotsтАЭ is also suggested by her hundred chariots in 7c.

The referent of y├й in c and the affiliation of that rel. cl. are disputed. Geldner takes the rel. pronoun as referring to the r├бth─Бn─Бm of b. This has the merit of associating the rel. with an adjacent noun in the proper number and gender and keeping the relative clause syntactically confined to the verse in which it appears. However, it affords these chariots more agency and significance than I think they deserve. Instead, the rel. cl. of cd seems to group more naturally with the identically structured y├й clause in 4ab, which also has a 3rd pl. presential reflexive verb preceded by a loc. pl.

and also contains a genitive referrring to Dawn. The two clauses also begin with a metrically irregular 11-syllable p─Бda with a rest right before the caesura, an irregularity that also speaks for their association. This pair of relative clauses is resolved by the main clause in 4cd. Such an enjambed structure is characteristic of prag─Бthas. (Renou also take the two verses this way.) Then there is the question of the meaning of dadhrir├й. It belongs to the root тИЪdhс╣Ы тАШhold, supportтАЩ, and in this (rare) middle usage seems to have reflexive value тАШhold oneselfтАЩ/тАШhold oneself fastтАЩ, with the possible pregnant sense тАШhold oneself readyтАЩ (so Renou, Witzel Got┼Н, Geldner n.). I take it as having slightly different meanings in simile and frame (a favored poetic strategy of Vedic bards). In the simile it depicts sailors (or some sort of boatsmen) standing firm against the rigors of the voyage, whereas in the frame the subjects (who are identified in the parallel rel. clause of 4ab as patrons) hold themselves ready to give, an action that is also the topic of that parallel rel.

clause. In fact, one could almost construe (or supply) the d─Бn─Б╠Бya of 4b with dadhrir├й as well as with its own clause.

+Griffith

Usas hath dawned, and now shall dawn, the Goddess, driver forth of cars
Which, as she cometh nigh, have fixed their thought on her, like glory-seekers on the flood.

Sie hat gestrahlt und strahle nun, die Morgeng├╢ttin, Treiberin Der Wagen, die die Bahn verfolgen, wenn sie naht, wie Schatzbegier’ge auf dem Meer.

рд╣реЗ рдЙрд╖рдГ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдпрд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рдЧрдордиреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рддреНрд╕реБ рдпреЗ рд╕реВрд░рдпрдГ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рджрд╛рдирд╛рднрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ рджрд╛рдирд╛рдп рдзрдирд╛рджрд┐рджрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдордирдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░ рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬрддреЗ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ред рджрд╛рдирд╢реАрд▓рд╛ рдЙрджрд╛рд░рд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рднрд╡рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГрдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рджрд╛рддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рджрд╛рддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрддрд╛рдВ рдиреГрдгрд╛рдВ рддрддреН рдирд╛рдо рджрд╛рдирд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗ рд▓реЛрдХрдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рдирд╛рдо рдХрдгреНрд╡рддрдордГ рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡реА рдХрдгреНрд╡рдГ рдорд╣рд░реНрд╖рд┐рдГ рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд╣ рдЕрддреНрд░реИрд╡ рдЙрд╖рдГрдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдЧреГрдгрд╛рддрд┐ рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ ред рдпреЛ рджрд╛рддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдпрд╢реНрдЪ рдирд╛рдордЧреНрд░рд╣рдгреЗрди рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рддрд┐ рддрд╛рд╡реБрднрд╛рд╡рдкреНрдпреБрд╖рдГрдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдПрд╡ рддрдерд╛ рдХреБрд░реБрдд рдЗрддреНрдпреБрд╖рд╕рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ рее рдЧреГрдгрд╛рддрд┐ ред тАШрдЧреД рд╢рдмреНрджреЗ’ред рдХреНрд░реИрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГ ред тАШ рдкреНрд╡рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рд╣реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╣рд╕реНрд╡рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдиреГрдгрд╛рдореН ред рдирд╛рдорд┐ тАШрдиреГ рдЪ ’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рем. рек. рем ) рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ ред рдиреГ рдЪрд╛рдиреНрдпрддрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рем. рез. резреорек ) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддреЗрд░реБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬUс╣гas, at your comings wise men turn their minds to benefactions; of these men, the most wise Kaс╣Зva proclaims the fame.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

And, o Dawn, those who at your journeys yoke their mind for givingтАФ the patronsтАФ
here (the poet) Kaс╣Зva, the latest of Kaс╣Зvas, sings their names, the names of those superior men.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse is somewhat oddly constructed, especially the distribution of elements in cd. The opening of c, ├бtr─Б╠Бha t├бd, seems overburdened with functionless elements, esp. the t├бd, which has no obvious referent. As it turns out, this opening is found elsewhere (I.135.8, 154.6), with a likewise referent-less t├бd. I therefore assume that the t├бd here emphasizes the temporal/logical ├бtra. Then we find two gen. plurals, eс╣г─Бm and nс╣Эс╣З─Б╠Бm, separated from each other, but probably ultimately coreferential. I assume that enclitic eс╣г─Бm serves as the correlative for y├й in p─Бda a (though we might expect t├йс╣г─Бm) and that the unusually heavy opening of the p─Бda has bumped it into pseudo-second position after the first real word of the clause, k├бс╣Зvaс╕е. But until we understand more about the interaction of the placement of these various elements, this is simply an after-the-fact description. It should be noted that eс╣г─Бm generally does not show the standard WackernagelтАЩs Position behavior (modified 2nd position) that we might expect from an enclitic, and in particular has a tendency to take final position. The nс╣Эс╣З─Б╠Бm at the end of the verse simply doubles and further specifies eс╣г─Бm.

I have tr. n─Б╠Бma twice, for ease of English.

+Griffith

Here Kanva, chief of Kanva’s race, sings forth aloud the glories of the heroes’ names,–
The. princes who, O Usas, as thou comest near, direct their thoughts to liberal gifts.

+Geldner

O Usas! Kanva, der erste der Kanva┬┤s, preist hier den Namen der M├дnner die als freigebige Patrone bei deiner Ausfahrt ihren Sinn aufs Schenken einstellen.

+Grassmann

Der F├╝rsten, die, o Morgenroth, bei deinem Nahn zum Schenken wenden ihren Sinn, Ja deren Namen preiset hier der Kanvaspross, der M├дnner Kanva-├дhnlichster.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬUс╣гas, nourishing (all), comes daily like a matron, the directress (of household duties), conducting all transient (creatures) to decay; (at her coming) each biped stirs and she wakes up the birds.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Liberal-spirited Dawn drives here, giving delight like a maiden.
Wakening the footed community, she speeds along. She makes the
winged ones fly up.

+Griffith

Like a good matron Usas comes carefully tending everything:
Rousing all life she stirs all creatures that have feet, and makes the birds of air fly up.

+Geldner

Die Usas kommt Gutes tuend wie eine edle junge Frau. Die Schar dessen, was F├╝├Яe hat, erweckend naht sie; die V├╢gel treibt sie zum Aufflug.

+Grassmann

Erfreuend kommt das Morgenroth, wie eine jugendliche Maid; Was F├╝sse hat, zum Werk erweckend eilet sie und treibt zum Flug die V├╢gel an.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda depicts the usual effect of Dawn - sending all creatures on their daily business.

├│dat─л: Though this form appears to be a fem. pres. participle to a Class I present (also in its other occurrence VIII.69.2), such an analysis is formally troublesome, because the feminine stem is weak (-at-─л), though a strong suffix is expected in Class I (e.g., bh├бvant─л-). Moreover, there are no other forms to the putative present *├│dati; the standard present is nasal-infix un├бtti with transitive value.

And ├│dat─л- lacks participial sense: it simply means тАШwetтАЩ. It thus seems best to take it as a non-participial -ant- adjective (as j├бrant- is often interpreted). It is worth noting that Whitney (Roots) classifies it as a primary derivative of the root and gives no Class I present and that Got┼Н makes no mention of it in his monograph on Class I; it is likewise undiscussed in LoweтАЩs monograph on RVic participles.

As for its meaning here, it is used simultaneously in two senses: the literal one, тАШwetтАЩ, referring to the dew characteristic of early morning, and тАШlubriciousтАЩ, referring to DawnтАЩs notorious hyperfeminine and sexual qualities, also reflected in 5ab y├│с╣гeva тАж prabhu├▒jat─л╠БтАЬgiving delight like a maiden.тАЭ v─Бj├нn─лvant- (also v─Бj├нn─л-vasu-). This fairly common adjective is obviously a derivative of extremely well-attested v─Бj├нn- тАШprize-winning (horse)тАЩ, itself a possessive adjective formed to v─Б╠Бja- тАШprizeтАЩ. The usual tr. of v─Бj├нn─лvant- are rather attenuated тАФ Grassmann тАШgabenreichтАЩ, Geldner (here) тАШdu ReichbelohnendeтАЩ, Debrunner (AiG II.2.

  1. тАЩgabenreichтАЩ тАФ or render it as if it were identical to v─Б╠Бja-vant-; so Renou (here) тАШporteuse des prix de victoireтАЩ, Witzel Got┼Н тАШdu RennpreisbesitzendeтАЩ. By contrast, I feel that both the apparent feminine v─Бj├нn─л and the second possessive suffix (-vant- in addition to -in-) should be noted and I interpret the stem as meaning тАШpossessing prizewinning maresтАЩ. v─Бj├нn─лvant- is esp. characteristic of Dawn and other female figures (e.g., Sarasvat─л), who might be expected to have female animals; though v─Бj╠Бin─л-vasuis almost entirely confined to the A┼Ыvins, those gods are very closely associated with Dawn. Debrunner (AiG II.2.409) instead ascribes the -─л- to тАЬErweiterung durch -─лnach Analogie anderer W├╢rter,тАЭ but doesnтАЩt in this case suggest what other word(s) might be involved.

тАЬThis auspicious Uс╣гas has harnessed (her vehicles) from afar, above the rising of the sun; and she comes gloriously upon man, with a hundred chariots.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

This one has hitched herself up from out of the distance, from (the place of) the rising of the sun.
With a hundred chariots, this well-portioned Dawn drives out
toward men.

+Griffith

This Dawn hath yoked her steeds afar, beyond the rising of the Sun:
Borne on a hundred chariots she, auspicious Dawn, advances on her way to Men.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAll living beings adore her, that she may be visible; bringer of good, she lights up the world; the affluent daughter of heaven drives away the malevolent and disperses the absorbers (of moisture).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sridhaс╕е: ┼Ыoс╣гayitс╣Ыn = the driers up; an allusion to the clouds which take up the dew of night?

+Jamison Brereton

Every moving creature bows before her gaze. The spirited one
creates light. Dawn, the bounteous Daughter of Heaven, dawns away hatred, away failures.

+Griffith

To meet her glance all living creatures bend them down: Excellent One, she makes the light.
Usas, the Daughter of the Sky, the opulent, shines foes and enmities away.

+Geldner

Alles was lebt, beugt sich ihrem Anblick; Licht macht die Edle. Die freigebige Tochter des Himmels Usas soll die Anfeindung, die Fehlschl├дge hinweg leuchten.

+Grassmann

Es neigt die ganze Welt sich ihrem Anblick zu, die jugendliche schaffet Licht; Die reiche Himmelstochter strahle weg den Hass, die Feinde weg das Morgenroth.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬShine around, Uс╣гas, with cheering lustre, bringing us every day much happiness, and scattering darkness.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Dawn, be radiant here with your glittering radiance, o Daughter of Heaven,
conveying hither abundant good fortune for us, dawning forth at the rituals of daybreak.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take the injunctive uchat as a modal (Geldner тАЬsoll тАж hinweg leuchtenтАЭ), but since this verb is parallel to a presential perfect n─Бn─Бma (so K├╝mmel 278- 79, pace Witzel Got┼Н тАЬhat sich тАж gebeutтАЭ) and a pres. indic. kс╣Ыс╣Зoti, I see no reason to ascribe modal value to uchat.

+Griffith

Shine on us with thy radiant light, O Usas, Daughter of the Sky,
Bringing to us great store of high felicity, and beaming on our solemn rites.

+Geldner

Usas! Leuchte her mit deinem schimmernden Licht, Tochter des Himmels! Viel Gl├╝ck bringe uns mit, wenn du bei den Opfern des heutigen Tages aufleuchtest!

+Grassmann

O Himmelstochter strahle her mit hellem Glanz, o Morgenroth, Und f├╝hre du uns vieles sch├╢ne Gl├╝ck herbei, aufleuchtend bei dem Opferfest.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬInasmuch, bringer of good, as you dawn, the breath and life of all (creatures) rest in you; diffuser of light, come to us with your spacious car; possessor of wondrous wealth, hear our invocation.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

For the breathing and living of all is in you, when you dawn forth, spirited one.
With your lofty chariot, radiant one, heed our call, you of bright
bounty.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation тАЬwith your lofty chariot тАж heed our callтАЭ implies that the chariot is the instrument of her hearing. This was not the intent: the chariot is simply one of her attributes.

+Griffith

For in thee is each living creature’s breath and life, when, Excellent! thou dawnest forth.
Borne on thy lofty car, O Lady of the Light, hear, thou of wondrous wealth, our call.

+Geldner

Denn Atmen und Leben der ganzen Welt ist in dir, wenn du aufleuchtest, du Edle. Auf hohem Wagen erh├╢re du unseren Ruf, du strahlende mit pr├дchtigen Gaben!

+Grassmann

Denn jedes Wesens Hauch und Leben ist in dir, wenn du erstrahlst, o herrliche; Die du mit hohem Wagen hell dich zeigst, h├╢r, gabenreiche, unsern Ruf,

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬUс╣гas, accept the (sacrificial) food which of many kinds exists among the human race, and thereby bring to the ceremony the pious, who offering oblations, praise you.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Dawn, do win the prize, which is bright for the human race.
With it convey those of good action [=gods] here to the ceremonies, to those of good action [=sacrificers] who (as oblation-)conveyors sing to you.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

sukс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е is multiply ambiguous. Though it literally means тАШdoing/performing wellтАЩ / тАШof good actionтАЩ, it is ordinarily specialized for performing the sacrifice well and refers to the human actors in the ritual. However, it can also on occasion be used of gods (e.g., X.63.9). In this passage most tr. take it as a gen. sg. referring to the sacrificer and dependent on adhvar─Б╠Бn (e.g., Geldner тАЬzu den Opfern des FrommenтАЭ).

However, this leaves ─Б╠Бvaha without an object. I therefore read sukс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е as acc. pl., and in fact I read it so twice тАФ once as obj. of ─Б╠Бvaha and referring to gods (so also Grassmann) and once as the goal of ─Б╠Бvaha and referring to the mortal sacrificers. The first reading seems confirmed by the first p─Бda of the next verse, 12a, which тАЬrepairsтАЭ the less clear expression with v├н┼Ыv─Бn dev─Б╠Бm╠Р─Б╠Бvaha, using the same verb. The second reading, referring to the sacrificers, allows the y├й of 11d to have an antecedent of the right grammatical number. It would of course be possible to take sukс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е only once, as referring to the gods, assuming the gapping of a pronominal antecedent to y├й, but this loses the neat equation of gods and sacrificers.

+Griffith

O Usas, win thyself the strength which among men is wonderful.
Bring thou thereby the pious unto holy rites, those who as priests sing praise to thee.

+Geldner

So gewinne denn, o Usas, den Siegerpreis, der unter dem Menschenvolk Aufsehen macht! Mit dem fahre her zu den Opfern des Frommen, zu den Opferleitern, die dich preisen!

+Grassmann

Gib Reichthum denn, o Morgenroth, der herrlich bei den Menschen gl├дnzt, Mit diesem fahre zu des Frommen Opfern her, zu dem, der dir Ges├дnge weiht.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬUс╣гas, bring from the firmament all the gods, to drink the Soma, and to you yourself bestow upon us excellent and invigorating food, along with cattle and horses.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Convey all the gods here for soma-drinking from the midspace, o Dawn. Establish in us a mass of cows and of horses, worthy of praise, o Dawn, also victoryтАЩs prize and good heroes en masse.

+Griffith

Bring from the firmament, O Usas, all the Gods, that they may drink our Soma juice,
And, being what thou art, vouchsafe us kine and steeds, strength meet for praise and hero might.

+Geldner

Alle G├╢tter fahr zum Somatrunk aus dem Luftreich her, o Usas! Bring du uns Rinderbesitz, Rossebesitz, preislichen, o Usas, den Ehrenpreis und die Meisterschaft!

+Grassmann

Zum Somatrunke fahr die G├╢tter alle her, o Morgenr├╢the, aus der Luft, Und gib uns werthes ross- und rinderreiches Gut und Heldenkraft, o Morgenroth.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAdorable Uс╣гas, whom the ancient sages invoked for protection and for food, do you, (radiant) with pure light, (plural ased) by our offerings, accept our praises.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Because even those previous seers who called upon you for aid, for help, o great oneтАФ
do you (now) greet our praises (as you did theirs) with generosity, o Dawn, with your bright brilliance.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The relative clause of ab (lit. тАЬwhich previous seers тАжтАЭ y├й тАж с╣Ы╠Бс╣гayaс╕е p┼л╠БrveтАж) has no explicit referent in the main clause, but implicit is the notion that our praises should receive the same favorable response from Dawn as theirs did, so there is a suppressed gen. pl. t├йс╣г─Бm or the like. The other passage containing the 3rd pl. mid.

pf. juh┼лr├й (VIII.8.6) is constructed almost identically to this one, though in dimeter meter, with a similar implicit understanding of the relation between subordinate cl.

and main cl.

+Griffith

Mighty One, whom the Rsis of old time invoked for their protection and their help,
O Usas, graciously answer our songs of praise with bounty and with brilliant light.

+Geldner

So viele Rishi┬┤s auch dich fr├╝her zur Hilfe, zur Gunst angerufen haben, du Gro├Яe, so erkenne du unsere Preislieder durch eine Ehrengabe an, o Usas, mit deinem hellen Feuerschein!

+Grassmann

Wie du von fr├╝hern S├дngern auch gerufen bist zum Schutz, o grosse, und zur Huld; So lohne mit Geschenken unsern Lobgesang, und hellem Licht, o Morgenroth.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬUс╣гas, since you have today set upon the two gates of heaven with light, grant us a spacious and secure habitation; bestow upon us, goddess, cattle and food.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Dawn, when today with your radiance you will push apart the two doors of heaven,
then hold out to us broad shelter that keeps the wolf away, o goddess, hold out refreshments consisting of cows.

+Griffith

Usas, as thou with light to day hast opened the twin doors of heaven,
So grant thou us a dwelling wide and free from foes. O Goddess, give us food with kine.
